sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Deadline is reporting that <strong>Michael Rapaport</strong>, an actor I don&#8217;t think I&#8217;ve seen in anything in a very long time, will star in a TV series about the &#8220;rise, fall and subsequent rise of famous shoe designer and entrepreneur Steve Madden.&#8221; Madden &#8220;took his company, which makes ?his eponymous shoe brand, from the fledgling startup he founded thirty years ago with a mere $1,100 to a global juggernaut,&#8221; but also ended up with a &#8220;criminal conviction and a prison sentence after his financial affairs got entangled with the brokerage house Stratton Oakmont, co-founded by Madden’s childhood friend Danny Porush.&#8221; Part of this story was actually covered in the Martin Scorsese movie <em>The Wolf of Wall Street</em>. The series will adapt Madden&#8217;s book <i>The Cobbler: How I Disrupted An Industry, Fell From Grace &#38; Came Back Stronger Than Ever</i><em>, </em>but I&#8217;m guessing they&#8217;ll change the name since everyone associates <em>The Cobbler</em> with that terrible Adam Sandler movie.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/percyjackson-trio-hiding.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-621228\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/percyjackson-trio-hiding-700x332.jpg\" alt=\"Percy Jackson Author Hates the Movies\" width=\"700\" height=\"332\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/percyjackson-trio-hiding-700x332.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/percyjackson-trio-hiding-360x171.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/percyjackson-trio-hiding-768x365.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/percyjackson-trio-hiding.jpg 1053w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong><em>Percy Jackson</em></strong>, one of those YA series that I know next to nothing about, is getting another adaptation courtesy of a Disney+ series. And Rick Riordan, who wrote the book series, says Disney is currently in the midst of looking for their lead. &#8220;We are looking for the best person who can embody the character we all know and love from the books,&#8221; he wrote (via Deadline). &#8220;As with all casting choices, we will be following Disney’s company policy, which says: We are committed to diverse, inclusive casting. For every role, please submit qualified performers, without regard to disability, gender, race and ethnicity, age, color, national origin, sexual orientation, gender identity or any other basis prohibited by law.&#8221; In the books, Percy Jackson is an eighteen-year-old Greek demigod, the son of Poseidon and Sally Jackson.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/noah-centineo-e1619791887591.jpeg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-669302\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/noah-centineo-e1619791887591-700x299.jpeg\" alt=\"masters of the universe\" width=\"700\" height=\"299\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/noah-centineo-e1619791887591-700x300.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/noah-centineo-e1619791887591-360x154.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/noah-centineo-e1619791887591.jpeg 736w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Deadline is reporting that <strong>Noah Centineo</strong>, of <em>To All The Boys&#8230;</em> fame, is set to star in a CIA series at Netflix. The show finds Centineo as &#8220;a fledgling lawyer at the CIA who becomes enmeshed in dangerous international power politics when a former asset threatens to expose the nature of her long-term relationship with the agency, unless they exonerate her of a serious crime.&#8221; The series has received an eight-episode order and comes from <em>The Rookie</em> creator <strong>Alexi Hawley</strong> who will serve as showrunner.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/8_e-qFKgrcs?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>HBO&#8217;s <strong><em>Betty</em> </strong>is returning for a second season in June, and you can watch the trailer above. In the series, &#8220;As Kirt (<strong>Nina Moran</strong>), Janay (<strong>Dede Lovelace</strong>), Honeybear (<strong>Moonbear</strong>), Camille (<strong>Rachelle Vinberg</strong>), and Indigo (<strong>Ajani Russell)</strong> cross the threshold to womanhood, they unite to protect and empower their skate community, fearlessly mining the nuances of their identities and embracing their differences along the way. Independent, strong-willed, and discerning, these women are brought together by skateboarding – but their bond goes far beyond the sport.&#8221; The show was inspired by the film <em>Skate Kitchen</em>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/game-of-thrones-the-dragon-and-the-wolf-1-e1504100745708.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-437707\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/game-of-thrones-the-dragon-and-the-wolf-1-e1504100745708-700x336.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"336\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/game-of-thrones-the-dragon-and-the-wolf-1-e1504100745708-700x336.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/game-of-thrones-the-dragon-and-the-wolf-1-e1504100745708-360x173.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/game-of-thrones-the-dragon-and-the-wolf-1-e1504100745708.jpg 1200w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong><em>Scary Stories For Young Foxes</em></strong>, which is not the fourth book in the <em>Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark</em> franchise despite its name, is becoming an animated series. The book by Christian McKay Heidicker is a &#8220;coming-of-age tale of two young foxes, born of different families, whose youthful misfortunes bring them together. The eight interconnected stories explore the power of scary tales, why we tell them and how we react to them.&#8221; <strong>Lena Headey</strong> will produce the show through her Boat Rocker Studios, and she&#8217;ll also voice one of the characters, per Deadline.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/UbtNbtWqrx4?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>HBO Max has a new comedy series with <em>Saturday Night Live</em>&#8216;s <strong>Michael Che</strong>. Called <strong><em>That Damn Michael Che</em></strong>, it&#8217;s described as a &#8220;groundbreaking new comedy series where each episode illustrates what it feels like to experience everyday situations including racial profiling, unemployment, falling in love, and more, from Michael&#8217;s perspective.&#8221; Cecily Strong, Heidi Gardner, Colin Quinn, Ellen Cleghorne, and Colin Jost all appear on the show, along with guest stars Omari Hardwick, Geoffrey Owens, Godfrey, Billy Porter and Method Man. You can stream all six episodes of <em>That Damn Michael Che</em><strong> May 6</strong> on HBO Max.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/Aj8ua1zQPSs?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p><strong><em>The Kominsky Method</em></strong> is a series that continues to seem fake. I know it&#8217;s a real show, of course – but I don&#8217;t know a single person who has ever watched it. It&#8217;s almost like the show is some sort of mafia front for criminal activity or something. Anyway, the show is returning for its third and final season, and you can watch the trailer above, and then watch the season when it arrives on <strong>May 28</strong>. But be honest: you&#8217;re not going to watch it. No one is. It doesn&#8217;t exist.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/zachary-levi-marvelous-mrs.-maisel.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-487975\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/zachary-levi-marvelous-mrs.-maisel-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"zachary levi marvelous mrs. maisel\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/zachary-levi-marvelous-mrs.-maisel.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/zachary-levi-marvelous-mrs.-maisel-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Deadline says that <strong><em>The Marvelous Mrs. Maisel</em> </strong>season 4 has added<strong> Reid Scott</strong> and <strong>Gideon Glick</strong> in recurring roles. Who are they playing? We don&#8217;t know yet, sorry. The Amazon series, which follows a housewife who becomes a stand-up comedian in the 1950s, is currently in production in New York.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theduchess-katherineryan-middlefinger.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-631871\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theduchess-katherineryan-middlefinger-700x312.jpg\" alt=\"The Duchess Trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"312\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theduchess-katherineryan-middlefinger-700x312.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theduchess-katherineryan-middlefinger-360x161.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theduchess-katherineryan-middlefinger-768x343.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/theduchess-katherineryan-middlefinger.jpg 914w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong><em>The Duchess</em></strong>, a series I confess I&#8217;ve never even heard of, has been canceled by Netflix after one season. The series followed &#8220;A fashionably disruptive single mother navigates life, love, and the question of whether or not to have another child with her nemesis: her ex, the father of her daughter.&#8221; Series creator <strong>Katherine Ryan</strong> said (via <a href=\"https://www.comingsoon.net/tv/news/1171610-netflix-cancels-the-duchess\">Coming Soon</a>): &#8220;[Netflix] didn’t want to make any more, not enough people watched it. I think something like 10 million people watched it in 28 days and that wasn’t enough. But also, I’m not terribly sad about it. I feel like it’s a whole lot of work, a whole lot of time to make a sitcom. I was so grateful to able to make it, but I think it speaks for itself. I kind of like the way it ended.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/The-Conners-live-episode.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-601864\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/The-Conners-live-episode-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"The Conners live episode\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/The-Conners-live-episode.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/The-Conners-live-episode-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s actually pretty amazing that there was a revival of <em>Rosanne</em> that killed off the Rosanne character (due to the real Rosanne&#8217;s offensive tweets), and then managed to keep on going for multiple seasons. But that&#8217;s what happened, and <strong><em>The Conners</em></strong>, as the show was rebranded, is now officially returning for season 4. The lead actors are all expected to return, and Deadline adds the plan is to have a 20-episode season.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/let-the-right-one-in-700.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-285436\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/let-the-right-one-in-700-700x306.jpg\" alt=\"Let the Right One In TV series\" width=\"700\" height=\"306\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/let-the-right-one-in-700.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/let-the-right-one-in-700-360x157.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>The <em>Let the Right One In</em> TV series, based on the John Ajvide Lindqvist novel that&#8217;s been adapted into a movie twice, has added<strong> Grace Gummer</strong> to its cast. Gummer joins <strong>Demián Bichir</strong> and <strong>Anika Noni Rose </strong>in the vampire TV series, which follows (per <a href=\"https://collider.com/let-the-right-one-in-show-cast-grace-gummer/\">Collider</a>) &#8220;the lives of Mark (Bichir) and his 12-year-old daughter Eleanor. 10 years earlier, Eleanor was turned into a vampire, and her father keeps her locked away for her safety and the safety of others. A homicide detective and single mother Naomi (Rose) moves in next door with a son the same age. Bullied by his peers, Isiah and Eleanor quickly become friends as they bond over their outcast status.&#8221; Gummer will play &#8220;Claire, the heiress of a pharmaceutical company who rejects the family business in order to pursue more noble disease research. Her life is forever changed when her estranged, dying father reveals a terrible secret.&#8221; The series is headed to Showtime, although there&#8217;s no premiere date just yet.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/-0beFQnB5lY?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>In the second half of<strong> <em>Lucifer</em></strong> season 5, &#8220;God himself comes to Earth. Secrets will be revealed, heroic sacrifices will be made, and the world will never be the same.&#8221; The series has had quite a ride, starting on Fox before going to Netflix. It&#8217;s also already been renewed for a sixth and final season, so you&#8217;ll have that to look forward to if you&#8217;re a fan. The second half of season 5 hits Netflix on <strong>May 28</strong>.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/emilyinparis-lilycollins-camera-friend.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-636655\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/emilyinparis-lilycollins-camera-friend-700x313.jpg\" alt=\"Emily in Paris\" width=\"700\" height=\"313\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/emilyinparis-lilycollins-camera-friend-700x313.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/emilyinparis-lilycollins-camera-friend-360x161.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/emilyinparis-lilycollins-camera-friend-768x343.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/emilyinparis-lilycollins-camera-friend.jpg 966w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong><em>Emily in Paris</em></strong>, a series everyone claimed to hate and then watched anyway, is currently in production on its second season. Netflix announced this news along with the tidbit that the show was their most popular comedy of 2020. So maybe stop hate watching this show if you genuinely don&#8217;t like it, kids. The series stars<strong> Lily Collins</strong> and is about Chicago marketing executive Emily Cooper, who is &#8220;hired to provide an American perspective at a marketing firm in Paris.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/imdb-streaming-service.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-529822\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/imdb-streaming-service-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"imdb streaming service\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/imdb-streaming-service-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/imdb-streaming-service-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/imdb-streaming-service-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/imdb-streaming-service.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>IMDb TV is trying to make a name for themselves, and they&#8217;ve just ordered a slew of original shows, per Deadline. <strong>Mike Schur</strong>, creator of <em>The Good Place</em>, is teaming with writer <strong>Shea Serrano</strong> for &#8220;<strong><em>Primo</em></strong>, a coming-of-age story about a Mexican-American teenager balancing cultural norms, college aspirations, societal expectations and the hectic home life of being raised by his single mom and five uncles.&#8221; Then there&#8217;s <strong>Melina Kanakaredes</strong>&#8216; <strong><em>Greek Candy</em></strong>, &#8220;a single-camera comedy, from Sony Pictures Television, tells the story of mom, dad, their three teenage daughters, four very Greek immigrant grandparents, and one very non-Greek “adopted” son and what it means to live the American dream in 2021.&#8221; <strong>Nkechi Okoro Carroll</strong> is writing <em><strong>The Fed,</strong></em> &#8220;which follows both the personal and career drama surrounding a group of young finance hopefuls as they begin an elite fellowship with the Federal Reserve, the nation’s most powerful financial institution. These young financial geniuses are destined for greatness — provided they don’t screw it all up with secrets, lies, sex, and politics.&#8221; <strong><em>B</em><em>lessed and Highly Favored</em></strong><em> </em>is an &#8220;unconventional workplace following Christine Kimbrough, a prodigal daughter who returns to Dallas as a rookie pastor and is tasked with keeping her family’s church alive in the face of rival megachurches, money problems and the presence of her predecessor and toughest critic—her father, Robert.&#8221; And finally there&#8217;s <strong><em>The Pradeeps of Pittsburgh, PA</em></strong><em>, </em>which &#8220;follows an Indian family and the tumultuous yet humorous events of the two years since they arrived in Pittsburgh. Told as a comedic mystery for the audience to unravel, viewers discover what pushed them to the brink, leading to their present immigration woes.&#8221;</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Law-and-Order-Logo.jpeg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-670108\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Law-and-Order-Logo-700x394.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"394\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Law-and-Order-Logo-700x394.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Law-and-Order-Logo-360x203.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Law-and-Order-Logo-768x432.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Law-and-Order-Logo.jpeg 1000w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Looks like it&#8217;s time for yet another <em>Law &#38; Order </em>spin-off. This one, per Variety, is called <strong><em>Law &#38; Order: For the Defense</em></strong>, and &#8220;will take a look inside a criminal defense firm. The series will put the lawyers under the microscope, along with the criminal justice system with every week delivering the promise of a contemporary morality tale.&#8221; Dun dun.</p>\n<p>The post <a 22:15:53","updatedTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","title":"‘Army of the Dead’ Interactive Event Will Allow Fans to Unlock the First 15 Minutes of the Movie","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=670399","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-670404\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-1-e1620411083904-700x301.jpg\" alt=\"army of the dead event\" width=\"700\" height=\"301\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-1-e1620411083904-700x300.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-1-e1620411083904-360x155.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-1-e1620411083904-768x330.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-1-e1620411083904.jpg 1499w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Netflix is inviting fans to embark on a heist — of sorts — of their own. A global livestream event for <strong><em>Army of the Dead</em></strong> will allow fans to unlock the first 15 minutes of Zack Snyder&#8217;s zombie heist movie through an &#8220;interactive experience.&#8221; It&#8217;s not a heist featuring the undead and a <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/zack-snyders-army-of-the-dead-zombie-tiger/\">zombie tiger</a>, but it will do.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-670399\"></span></p>\n<p>Netflix announced that it will host aan interactive <em>Army of the Dead</em> event on Thursday, <strong>May 13, 2021</strong> at 10 A.M. PT/1  P.M. ET, available only on the <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZnDjXm8j-yU\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v%3DZnDjXm8j-yU&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1620491980636000&#38;usg=AFQjCNEXnQvwS1zsSxYWrfiX56GKVykk-A\">Netflix YouTube channel</a>. Fans can tune into this interactive experience to unlock the first 15 minutes of the zombie action heist flick and see special appearances from director Zack Snyder, as well as cast members Dave Bautista, Ella Purnell, Omari Hardwick, Ana De La Reguera, Matthias Schweighöfer, Nora Arnezeder, Tig Notaro and more.</p>\n<p>Once unlocked, audiences will have a 32 hour window to watch the beginning of <em>Army of The Dead</em> on the Netflix YouTube channel, which is &#8220;the same amount of time that Scott Ward (Dave Bautista) and his crew have to break into zombie-infested Las Vegas to retrieve the $200 million sitting in a vault beneath the strip before the city is nuked,&#8221; per Netflix. Netflix&#8217;s press release also says that fans will have to &#8220;dig&#8221; for the video, whatever that means.</p>\n<p>In <em>Army of the Dead</em>, &#8220;following a zombie outbreak that has left Las Vegas in ruins and walled off from the rest of the world. When Scott Ward (Dave Bautista), a displaced Vegas local, former zombie war hero who’s now flipping burgers on the outskirts of the town he now calls home, is approached by casino boss Bly Tanaka (<strong>Hiroyuki Sanada</strong>), it’s with the ultimate proposition: Break into the zombie-infested quarantine zone to retrieve $200 million sitting in a vault beneath the strip before the city is nuked by the government in 32 hours. Driven by the hope that the payoff could help pave the way to a reconciliation with his estranged daughter Kate (<strong>Ella Purnell</strong>), Ward takes on the challenge, assembling a ragtag team of experts for the heist. They include Maria Cruz (<strong>Ana de la Reguera</strong>), an ace mechanic and Ward’s old friend; Vanderohe (<strong>Omari Hardwick</strong>), a zombie killing machine; Marianne Peters (<strong>Tig Notaro</strong>), a cynical helicopter pilot; Mikey Guzman (<strong>Raúl Castillo</strong>), a go-for-broke influencer and Chambers (<strong>Samantha Win</strong>), his ride-or-die; Martin (<strong>Garret Dillahunt</strong>), the casino’s head of security; a badass warrior known as the Coyote (<strong>Nora Arnezeder</strong>) who recruits Burt Cummings (<strong>Theo Rossi</strong>), a slimy security guard; and a brilliant German safe cracker named Dieter (<strong>Matthias Schweighöfer</strong>). Scott finds an unexpected emotional hurdle when Kate joins the expedition to search for Geeta (<strong>Huma S. Qureshi</strong>), a mother who’s gone missing inside the city. With a ticking clock, a notoriously impenetrable vault, and a smarter, faster horde of Alpha zombies closing in, only one thing’s for certain in the greatest heist ever attempted: survivors take all.&#8221;</p>\n<p><em>Army of the Dead</em> opens in select theaters on Friday, <strong>May 14, 2021</strong>, followed by a Netflix debut on <strong>Friday, May 21.</strong> See a new poster for <em>Army of the Dead</em> below.</p>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-670403\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-700x1037.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"1037\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-700x1037.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/EN-US_AOTD_MAIN_Slots_Vertical_RGB_EN-US_Theatrical-338x500.jpg 338w, href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/army-of-the-dead-event-first-15-minutes/\">&#8216;Army of the Dead&#8217; Interactive Event Will Allow Fans to Unlock the First 15 Minutes of the Movie</a> appeared 22:15:53","updatedTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","title":"‘Time Cut’ Will Reunite ‘Freaky’ Creative Team For Movie Described as ‘Back to the Future’ Meets ‘Scream’","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=670377","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/time-cut.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-670384\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/time-cut-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"time cut\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/time-cut-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/time-cut-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/time-cut-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/time-cut.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Christopher Landon</strong> and <strong>Michael Kennedy</strong>, the team that recently worked together on the fantastic body-swap slasher comedy <em>Freaky</em>, are reuniting for yet another high-concept horror project. It&#8217;s called <strong><em>Time Cut</em></strong>, and it&#8217;s described as <em>Back to the Future</em> meets <em>Scream</em>. What more do you need to know, really? <strong>Madison Bailey</strong> and <strong>Antonia Gentry</strong> are set to star in the film, with Landon producing and Kennedy co-writing the script with Sono Patel. <em>Into the Dark </em>filmmaker <strong>Hannah Macpherson</strong> will direct, with production gearing up in June.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-670377\"></span></p>\n<p>One of my favorite movies from last year was <em>Freaky</em>, a funny, gory horror-comedy that blended slasher movie thrills with body-swap humor. It worked incredibly well, and that makes me all the more excited about <em>Time Cut</em>, a new film coming from the <em>Freaky</em> team. Christopher Landon, who co-wrote and directed <em>Freaky</em>, is set to produce <em>Time Cut</em>, while Michael Kennedy, who co-wrote the <em>Freaky</em> screenplay, is handling the <em>Time Cut</em> script with Sono Patel (<em>The Marvelous Mrs. Maisel</em>). Hannah Macpherson, who helmed the <em>Into the Dark</em> entry <em>Pure</em>, will direct.</p>\n<p>While we don&#8217;t have a full synopsis, <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/movies/movie-news/madison-bailey-antonia-gentry-movie-to-all-the-boys-producer-exclusive-1234947285/\">THR</a> describes the film as &#8220;<em>Back to the Future</em> meets <em>Scream</em>,&#8221; which sounds like a great idea overall. By this description we can surmise that both time travel and murder are going to be on display here, and we all love time travel and murder, don&#8217;t we, folks? Also, maybe someone  in the movie will invent rock and roll at a school dance.</p>\n<p>THR is also calling this a &#8220;YA movie,&#8221; which means it probably won&#8217;t be as gory as <em>Freaky</em>, but that&#8217;s okay. Landon has worked with a slasher movie crossed with time travel before, sort of, with the <em>Happy Death Day</em> movies. Now if only someone would go ahead and let him make <em>Happy Death Day 3</em>, gosh darn it. And while we&#8217;re at it, let&#8217;s get a <em>Freaky </em>sequel. Why not? I&#8217;d watch it, and you probably would too. Perhaps if <em>Time Cut</em> is super successful it will give Landon and Kennedy all the ammunition they need to return to that franchise (if they even want to).</p>\n<p>Netflix stars Madison Bailey (<em>Outer Banks</em>) and Antonia Gentry (<em>Ginny &#38; Georgia</em>) will star in the movie. Matt Kaplan&#8217;s ACE Entertainment, which produces the <em>To All the Boys</em> series, is also producing the movie. Production on <em>Time Cut</em> is expected to begin in Canada this June. There&#8217;s no word yet where the film will end up – either in theaters or a streaming service – so stay tuned for updates.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/time-cut/\">&#8216;Time Cut&#8217; Will Reunite &#8216;Freaky&#8217; Creative Team For Movie Described as &#8216;Back to the Future&#8217; Meets &#8216;Scream&#8217;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 22:15:53","updatedTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","title":"Sony’s New ‘Cinderella’ Musical with Camila Cabello Has Been Sold to Amazon","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=670343","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-670350 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cinderella-camilacabello-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Camila Cabello Cinderella\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cinderella-camilacabello.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cinderella-camilacabello-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Another theatrical release bites the dust. Even though movie theaters are slowly getting back to normal and studios are starting to release major movies for audiences to see on the big screen again, not every movie waiting in the wings is lucrative enough for a studio to risk spending the money on a theatrical release right now. That&#8217;s why Sony Pictures has sold their new adaptation of the classic fairytale <strong><em>Cinderella</em></strong>, starring recording artist <strong>Camila Cabello</strong>, to Amazon instead of releasing it in theaters.<span id=\"more-670343\"></span></p>\n<p>Deadline has the news on Sony&#8217;s <em>Cinderella</em> skipping theaters and heading to a release on Amazon Prime sometime this year. The movie has been sitting around waiting for a release, and it was previously thought the movie might make it to theaters in July. But Sony Pictures has weighed their options ad figured having one of the streaming services pick it up would likely be more cost effective for them, especially after selling off other titles like Kevin Hart&#8217;s <em>Fatherhood</em> and Lin-Manuel Miranda&#8217;s animated <em>Vivo</em> to Netflix. However, I wouldn&#8217;t expect the streaming service to stick with a July window since they&#8217;re already planning on making <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-tomorrow-war-trailer/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>The Tomorrow War</em> with Chris Pratt</a> their big summer movie that month.</p>\n<p>In this new take on <em>Cinderella</em>, singer Camila Cabello takes the title role while the cast is filled with some surprisingly great and even perplexing stars. <strong>Idina Menzel</strong> plays the wicked stepmother while <strong>Billy Porter</strong> takes the role of the fairy godmother. Then there are also roles for <strong>Pierce Brosnan</strong>, <strong>Minnie Driver</strong>, <strong>John Mulaney</strong>, <strong>James Corden</strong>, and hip hop artist <strong>Missy Elliot</strong>. What the hell is this movie?</p>\n<p>Well, with <em>Pitch Perfect</em> scribe and <em>Blockers</em> director <strong>Kay Cannon</strong> writing the the script and getting behind the camera, it should come as no surprise that this is actually a more contemporary version of the familiar <em>Cinderella</em> story. Apparently it features pop songs from contemporary recording artists and even some original songs by Camilla Cabello herself. Plus, Idina Menzel will be singing a bit too. Perhaps we could be looking at something like <em>A Knight&#8217;s Tale</em> crossed with <em>Ever After</em>.</p>\n<p>Cannon has proven to have a great comedic mind as she&#8217;s crafted movies with rich female characters. She may have stumbled a bit with the scripts for the <em>Pitch Perfect</em> sequels, but we&#8217;ll chalk that up to the studio forcing them to happen. Considering Cannon&#8217;s other previous efforts, which also include writing and producing for <em>30 Rock</em> and <em>New Girl</em>, this just might be worth our time.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/camila-cabello-cinderella-movie-heads-to-amazon/\">Sony&#8217;s New &#8216;Cinderella&#8217; Musical with Camila Cabello Has Been Sold to Amazon</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a making <em>Mission: Impossible</em> movies, but as Tom Cruise&#8217;s closest cinematic collaborator, he was also brought onto Paramount&#8217;s <em>Top Gun: Maverick</em> to help work on the script for that long-anticipated sequel. And in a recent Twitter Q&#38;A, McQuarrie <a href=\"https://collider.com/top-gun-maverick-christopher-mcquarrie/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said</a> <em>Top Gun 2</em> is &#8220;the best film I&#8217;ve been a part of. I cannot wait to see it unleashed on an audience.&#8221; McQuarrie has been behind some incredibly entertaining movies, so that quote should help <em>Top Gun</em> fans breathe a sigh of relief at the prospect of this sequel actually being good.</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-670086 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Cruise-on-a-train-700x793.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"793\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Cruise-on-a-train.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Cruise-on-a-train-360x408.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Speaking of McQuarrie and Cruise, they&#8217;re currently working on the next <em>Mission: Impossible</em> movies, which will feature Cruise returning to a train as an action setpiece for the first time in the franchise since the 1996 original. The big difference? The train sequence in De Palma&#8217;s movie was clearly enhanced by CG, and this one looks like a more modern-day Cruise stunt that was performed for real and appears to have been very dangerous.</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-670088 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Halloween-Kills-set-photo-700x853.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"853\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Halloween-Kills-set-photo.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Halloween-Kills-set-photo-360x439.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em><strong>Halloween Kills</strong></em> producer <strong>Ryan Freimann</strong> <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/COCHz09lq0V/?utm_source=ig_embed\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">shared</a> this image from the set of <strong>David Gordon Green</strong>&#8216;s upcoming sequel to the <em>Halloween</em> reboot. The car is a throwback to a vehicle that was featured in the original movie on the first night Michael Myers escaped, and coupled with that old school ambulance in the background, I think it&#8217;s safe to say this movie will feature a flashback to one of the key moments in the lives of The Shape and protagonist Laurie Strode (<strong>Jamie Lee Curtis</strong>).</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-520040 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/themeg-jasonstatham-swimming-700x310.jpg\" alt=\"The Meg Honest Trailer\" width=\"700\" height=\"310\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/themeg-jasonstatham-swimming-700x310.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/themeg-jasonstatham-swimming-360x159.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/themeg-jasonstatham-swimming-768x340.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/themeg-jasonstatham-swimming.jpg 838w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Prepare yourself for more shark punching action. In an interview with <a href=\"https://collider.com/the-meg-2-jason-statham-filming-start-date/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Collider</a>, <em>The Meg</em> star <strong>Jason Statham</strong> revealed that production on the sequel is going to begin early next year. &#8220;We&#8217;re gonna start shooting in January, if I get my dates right,&#8221; he said. &#8220;Ben Wheatley is the director, I&#8217;m very excited to work with him. I&#8217;m thrilled to get going, it&#8217;s been a while. We&#8217;ve been waiting around for the right scripts to come in and the right director to turn up, and we&#8217;ve got all those things and they&#8217;re all stacked up now&#8230;we have a great shorthand already. We&#8217;ve got similar taste. I like his movies, I think he&#8217;s a brilliant director. I think we&#8217;ve got a good shot at making something good.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-549102 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Detective-Pikachu-Early-Reaction-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"Detective Pikachu Early Reaction\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Detective-Pikachu-Early-Reaction-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Detective-Pikachu-Early-Reaction-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Detective-Pikachu-Early-Reaction-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Detective-Pikachu-Early-Reaction.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><em>Detective Pikachu</em> was meant to kick off a whole series of Pokemon movies, but when it comes to talk of a sequel, there&#8217;s been crickets for a long while now. Speaking with <a href=\"https://www.inverse.com/entertainment/justice-smith-hbo-max-generation-detective-pikachu\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Inverse</a>, star <strong>Justice Smith</strong> said that he would &#8220;love to participate in <em>Detective Pikachu 2</em>,&#8221; but he is not confident it will ever happen. &#8220;I think we have to just kind of bury our hopes. I don&#8217;t think it&#8217;s going to happen. I really hope so though. Honestly, I&#8217;m such a huge fan, who knows, who knows? I hope so.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-607273 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Andy-Garcia-president-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Andy Garcia president\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Andy-Garcia-president.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Andy-Garcia-president-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>This final entry is technically a remake and not a sequel, but bear with me anyway: Deadline reports that <em>Ocean&#8217;s Eleven</em> actor <strong>Andy Garcia</strong> is co-starring with singer <strong>Gloria Estefan</strong> in another remake of <strong><em>Father of the Bride</em></strong>, following in the footsteps of Spencer Tracy and Steve Martin. <strong>Gaz Alazraki</strong> (<em>We Are the Nobles</em>) is directing, and <em>Dora and the Lost City of Gold</em> actress <strong>Isabela Merced</strong> and <strong>Adria Arjona</strong> (<em>Pacific Rim Uprising</em>) are set to <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/movies/movie-news/isabela-merced-joins-father-of-the-bride-remake-exclusive-4175056/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">co-star</a> in a version that will tell this tried-and-true story through the lens of a Cuban American family.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/sequel-bits-top-gun-maverick-mission-impossible-7-the-meg-2-and-more/\">Sequel Bits: Top Gun: Maverick, Mission Impossible 7, The Meg 2, and More</a> appeared first on 39b77312c7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/fzercGFnsbY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn67@2020_3/2021/05/09/14-16-08-945_8bddcf165c3dba32.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1620569753474},{"createdTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","updatedTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","title":"‘Dracula’ Spin-Off ‘Renfield’ is an “Extremely Violent Comedy”","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=670266","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/renfield-movie.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-670269\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/renfield-movie-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"renfield movie update\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/renfield-movie-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/renfield-movie-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/renfield-movie-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/renfield-movie.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>As Universal continues to revive its classic monsters, several different titles have been announced. One such title is <strong><em>Renfield</em></strong>, a movie focused on Dracula&#8217;s bug-eating minion. And according to producer <strong>Robert Kirkman</strong>, <em>Renfield</em> is going to be a bit different from the other upcoming Universal movies. For one thing, it&#8217;s being described as an &#8220;extremely violent comedy.&#8221;</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-670266\"></span></p>\n<p>After the Dark Universe crashed and burned, it looked like Universal was truly clueless about what to do with its classic monsters. Then came Leigh Whannell&#8217;s <em>The Invisible Man</em>. The film was a big hit with audiences and critics alike, and it showed that you <em>could</em> bring these characters into the modern era if you hired someone who knows what they&#8217;re doing.</p>\n<p>Since <em>The Invisible Man</em> hit theaters, Universal has announced several different monster-related projects. There&#8217;s a new <em>Dracula</em> from Karyn Kusama; there&#8217;s <em>The Invisible Woman</em> from Elizabeth Banks; Ryan Gosling is starring in a new take on <em>The Wolfman</em>, which is being directed by <em>Invisible Man</em> helmer Leigh Whannell; Paul Feig’s <em>Dark Army</em>, which is said to feature classic Universal monsters; The Monster Mash, which is a musical that we don&#8217;t know much about just yet; an untitled film produced by Phil Lord and Christopher Miller starring Channing Tatum; and more.</p>\n<p>Another one of the titles is <em>Renfield</em>, a <em>Dracula</em>-adjacent film focused on the bug-eating lunatic who has a connection with Dracula in Bram Stoker&#8217;s novel, and who was played memorably by Dwight Frye in the 1931 <em>Dracula</em> movie and Tom Waits in <em>Bram Stoker&#8217;s Dracula</em>. Renfield is a memorable, but minor, character, which means he&#8217;s going to need some fleshing out for his own movie.</p>\n<p><em>The Tomorrow War</em> filmmaker <strong>Chris McKay</strong> is in talks to direct the <em>Renfield</em> movie, with <em>Rick and Morty</em> writer<strong> Ryan Ridley</strong> tackling the script. The idea for the film came from a pitch by Robert Kirkman, who is also producing the film. During an appearance on Kevin Smith’s <a href=\"https://podcasts.google.com/feed/aHR0cDovL3Ntb2RjYXN0LmNvbS9jaGFubmVscy9mYXRtYW4tb24tYmF0bWFuL2ZlZWQ/episode/dGFnOnNvdW5kY2xvdWQsMjAxMDp0cmFja3MvMTA0MTQ1NDM5OQ?sa=X&#38;ved=0CAUQkfYCahcKEwiYzMDEirXwAhUAAAAAHQAAAAAQBA&#38;hl=en-PH\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Fat Man Beyond</a> (via <a href=\"https://www.comingsoon.net/movies/news/1172502-robert-kirkman-universals-renfield-extremely-violent-comedy\">Coming Soon</a>), Kirkman shed some more light on what we can expect from the movie.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We’re doing this cool movie for Universal that&#8217;s a focus on Renfield,&#8221; Kirkman said. &#8220;It&#8217;s a story about him being Dracula&#8217;s henchman and how shitty a job that is. It’s a fun, extremely violent comedy because I’ve got a crutch, and it’s violence.&#8221;</p>\n<p>A comedy about Renfield being shitty at his job as Dracula&#8217;s henchman is a pretty damn funny idea, and my interest in this has just risen considerably. I also like knowing that Universal is willing to be flexible with these films, and not force them all into one mold – some can be horror, some can be comedies, some can be musicals. You&#8217;re dealing with supernatural monsters – the sky&#8217;s the limit here. Go nuts!</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/renfield-movie-update/\">&#8216;Dracula&#8217; Spin-Off &#8216;Renfield&#8217; is an &#8220;Extremely Violent Comedy&#8221;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Sciretta","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/muppets-kermit-bar-700x300.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn5@2020_3/2021/05/09/14-16-06-116_fdadb0ad1c6dce8b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn96@2020_2/2021/05/09/14-16-08-991_9a442e8760d02cd4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=-JiE-2EW1qI:GaUtndJscsk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn48@2020_1/2021/05/09/14-16-08-965_179b6e4c8f825ef4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn24@2020_1/2021/05/09/14-16-09-490_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=-JiE-2EW1qI:GaUtndJscsk:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn87@2020_3/2021/05/09/14-16-09-620_f8abfccc6f0bc1b5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/-JiE-2EW1qI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn48@2020_3/2021/05/09/14-16-09-242_ed99974fcf486b82.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1620569753475},{"createdTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","updatedTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","title":"Cinemark Signs Deals With 5 Major Hollywood Studios for Shorter Theatrical Windows","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=670376","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-620392\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cinemark-theater-screen.jpg\" alt=\"Cinemark Movie Theaters Reopening\" width=\"684\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cinemark-theater-screen.jpg 684w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/cinemark-theater-screen-360x158.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 684px) 100vw, 684px\" /></p>\n<p>Theaters aren&#8217;t dying — though it looks like they&#8217;ll be showing major studio releases for an even shorter time than before. Six months after <strong>Cinemark</strong> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/universal-cinemark-deal/\">struck a deal</a> with Universal Filmed Entertainment Group — which itself came a few months after Universal&#8217;s own deal with AMC Theatres — the exhibition chain has signed new pacts with five major Hollywood studios that could help shorten the theatrical window.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-670376\"></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://variety.com/2021/film/news/cinemark-theater-deals-vod-studios-1234968717/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Variety</a> reports that Cinemark, the third most popular movie theater chain in the United States (behind AMC and Regal), has struck new agreements with five major Hollywood studios: <strong>Warner Bros. Picture Group</strong>, <strong>The Walt Disney Company</strong>, <strong>Paramount Pictures</strong>, and <strong>Sony Pictures Entertainment</strong>.</p>\n<p>The terms of the deals were not disclosed, but considering the previous pact with Universal made in November, which enabled the studio to move new releases — barring box office hits that bring in more than $50 million — to premium video-on-demand platforms just 17 days after they open in theaters, we can expect these studios to enjoy a shorter theatrical window at Cinemark theaters.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Cinemark is thrilled to have reached new agreements with our major studio partners, and we are eager to continue providing movie fans an immersive, larger-than-life cinematic environment to see major upcoming films, ranging from the biggest blockbusters to specialty fare to family-friendly content,&#8221; said Cinemark CEO Mark Zoradi. &#8220;In our ongoing efforts to maximize attendance and box office during the pandemic and beyond, our goal is to provide the widest range of content with terms that are in the best long-term interests of Cinemark, our studio partners and moviegoers. We are pleased with these recent developments and are confident we are taking positive steps toward reigniting theatrical exhibition and evolving the industry for a post-pandemic landscape.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The coronavirus (COVID-19) pandemic has massively reshaped exhibition, with streaming platforms and PVOD thriving while theaters were forced to shutter. Studios pushed back many of their theatrical releases, but just as many were sent straight to streaming or home video, which led many to debate whether the long-predicted <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/will-movie-theaters-survive/\">death of theaters</a> was being accelerated. A few options have been suggested, including <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/moviegoing-post-pandemic-premium/\">premium theatrical experiences</a>, but Hollywood seems to be shifting to this shorter theatrical window.</p>\n<p>Already various studios appear to be moving toward this practice, partly in service to their new streaming platforms. Paramount has said that its films will <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/paramount-plus-movies-in-2022/\">debut on its streaming service Paramount</a>+ within 45 days of theatrical release. Warner Bros. made the controversial choice of releasing its 2021 theatrical slate <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/amc-responds-to-warner-bros-2021-plans/\">day-and-date</a> in theaters and HBO Max. These theatrical window deals between exhibition chains, which need theatrical releases to bring in audiences, and studios, which wish to save money on advertising while boosting their streaming services, seems to be the best compromise for both parties.</p>\n<p>As for Cinemark, the chain only said that &#8220;each deal has unique attributes specific to the individual studio that mutually benefits both parties.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/cinemark-theatrical-deals-hollywood-studios/\">Cinemark Signs Deals With 5 Major Hollywood Studios for Shorter Theatrical Windows</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 22:15:53","updatedTime":"2021-05-09 22:15:53","title":"‘Stay Frosty’: Idris Elba to Star in Action Movie From ‘Extraction’ Director","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=670386","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-670397 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Stay-Frosty-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Stay Frosty\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Stay-Frosty.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Stay-Frosty-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Idris Elba</strong> is continuing his push into action movie territory.</p>\n<p>The<em> Luther</em>,<em> The Wire</em>, and Marvel Cinematic Universe veteran is leading the ensemble of James Gunn&#8217;s explosive action film <em>The Suicide Squad</em> later this year, and now Elba is also set to star in a new action film called <em><strong>Stay Frosty</strong></em>, which hails from <em>Extraction</em> director <strong>Sam Hargrave</strong>.<br />\n<span id=\"more-670386\"></span></p>\n<p>Deadline reports that Warner Bros. has won a &#8220;wild spec auction&#8221; for the rights to <em>Stay Frosty</em>, shelling out more than a million dollars against low seven figures in the hopes that the project gets made. Here&#8217;s the pitch: &#8220;After miraculously surviving a bullet to the head, a man has to figure out who wants him dead and why. He needs to stop the assassin while still making it back home in time to spend Christmas with his son.&#8221;</p>\n<p>This is just one or two degrees away from &#8220;What if <em>Crank</em> protagonist Chev Chelios was a family man?&#8221;, which sounds like a hell of a good time at the movies to me. (And speaking of the <em>Crank</em> movies, while I really like Jason Statham&#8217;s work in that franchise, I think Elba could have been a great Chelios himself had the producers gone in a different direction.) But yeah, toss a determined, righteously motivated, and pissed-off Elba in a Christmas action movie setting, and I&#8217;m absolutely interested in seeing the shit hit the fan as he tries to get home to his family.</p>\n<p><strong>Tyler Marceca</strong> wrote the script. If you don&#8217;t recognize that name, you&#8217;re not alone: he hasn&#8217;t written anything that&#8217;s been produced yet, but he did write a script for another action movie called <em>The Disciple Program</em> which was purchased by Universal way back in 2012. At the time, Mark Wahlberg was lined up to star in that project for <em>The Imitation Game</em> director Morton Tyldum, but it never materialized and we haven&#8217;t heard anything about it since. So Marceca is a blank slate to us.</p>\n<p>Hargrave is on board to direct <em>Stay Frosty</em>, which is a fun but silly title – I hope Elba utters it as a Schwarzenegger-inspired punch line just after dispatching with the villain. He worked as a stunt man, stunt coordinator, and second unit director on several major action films of the past 15 years before launching onto every studio&#8217;s radar with <em>Extraction</em>, his feature directorial debut which evidently did great viewership numbers for Netflix. An <em>Extraction</em> sequel is <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/extraction-2-sequel-or-prequel/\">reportedly in development</a>, so we&#8217;ll have to see which of these movies makes it to the starting line first.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/stay-frosty/\">&#8216;Stay Frosty&#8217;: Idris Elba to Star in Action Movie From &#8216;Extraction&#8217; Director</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
